  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;

  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */

    align-items: center;

    text-decoration: none;

  textarea, select, input {

  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

<span class="line"><!---->Author: Victor Gomes &lt;<!----></span>





victorgomes@chromium.org

Date: Wed Mar 01 15:28:23 2023



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Wed Mar 01 15:28:23 2023<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





[maglev] Move stack check from Prologue to FunctionEntryStackCheck



<span class="line"><!---->[maglev] Move stack check from Prologue to FunctionEntryStackCheck<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The stack check can lazy deopt in the deferred code of the prologue.



<span class="line"><!---->The stack check can lazy deopt in the deferred code of the prologue.<!----></span>



<br>





The register allocator will try to spill all inputs to the



<span class="line"><!---->The register allocator will try to spill all inputs to the<!----></span>



<br>





DeoptInfo before emitting FunctionEntryStackCheck, but this is



<span class="line"><!---->DeoptInfo before emitting FunctionEntryStackCheck, but this is<!----></span>



<br>





too late if the deopt happens in the prologue. In particular,



<span class="line"><!---->too late if the deopt happens in the prologue. In particular,<!----></span>



<br>





any RegisterInput will be saved in the stack by the



<span class="line"><!---->any RegisterInput will be saved in the stack by the<!----></span>



<br>





SaveRegisterStateForCall, but it will be wrongly picked up by



<span class="line"><!---->SaveRegisterStateForCall, but it will be wrongly picked up by<!----></span>



<br>





the deoptimizer.



<span class="line"><!---->the deoptimizer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Since nothing runs between the prologue and FunctionEntryStackCheck.



<span class="line"><!---->Since nothing runs between the prologue and FunctionEntryStackCheck.<!----></span>



<br>





We can just run the stack check in the latter node codegen instead.



<span class="line"><!---->We can just run the stack check in the latter node codegen instead.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Unfortunately this entails that if we have a RegisterInput, this



<span class="line"><!---->Unfortunately this entails that if we have a RegisterInput, this<!----></span>



<br>





will always be spilled in the beginning of the function.



<span class="line"><!---->will always be spilled in the beginning of the function.<!----></span>



<br>





We should fix that in the future.



<span class="line"><!---->We should fix that in the future.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

Unfortunately, this issue isn't eligible for a VRP reward because it is considered an known issue, as there is demonstrable evidence we would have discovered this issue before the bug made it out of head, as evidenced by 



<span class="line"><!---->Unfortunately, this issue isn't eligible for a VRP reward because it is considered an known issue, as there is demonstrable evidence we would have discovered this issue before the bug made it out of head, as evidenced by <!----></span>





issue 1420572



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1420572" title="Crash in Builtins_PromiseResolveThenableJob"><!---->issue 1420572<!----></a>





 



<span class="line"><!----> <!----></span>





- that we had a clusterfuzz fuzzer that discovered this bug in head as well. 



<span class="line"><!---->- that we had a clusterfuzz fuzzer that discovered this bug in head as well. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Chrome VRP policies [1] also state that "we discourage testing against canary or trunk/head builds, because they don't undergo release testing and can exhibit short-lived regressions that are typically identified and fixed very quickly." This is demonstrated by clusterfuzz finding this issues in parallel or not long after your report. 



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome VRP policies [1] also state that "we discourage testing against canary or trunk/head builds, because they don't undergo release testing and can exhibit short-lived regressions that are typically identified and fixed very quickly." This is demonstrated by clusterfuzz finding this issues in parallel or not long after your report. <!----></span>



<br>





This topic has previously been discussed in 



<span class="line"><!---->This topic has previously been discussed in <!----></span>





https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1416795#c21



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1416795#c21"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1416795#c21<!----></a>





 and c#22



<span class="line"><!----> and c#22<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is not to say that we do not ever reward for bugs in head, but these are based on bugs that we don't expect that we would have discovered / have no evidence we would have discovered without the help of the external report. Often these rewards involve discussions with the developer in which they have conveyed the benefit of the report. The previous reports you note in 



<span class="line"><!---->This is not to say that we do not ever reward for bugs in head, but these are based on bugs that we don't expect that we would have discovered / have no evidence we would have discovered without the help of the external report. Often these rewards involve discussions with the developer in which they have conveyed the benefit of the report. The previous reports you note in <!----></span>





comment #15



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c15"><!---->comment #15<!----></a>





 as well as this one have collided with our own internal fuzzers. There is no doubt we would have discovered these issues.



<span class="line"><!----> as well as this one have collided with our own internal fuzzers. There is no doubt we would have discovered these issues.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Also, regarding your 



<span class="line"><!---->Also, regarding your <!----></span>





comment #15



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c15"><!---->comment #15<!----></a>





, it is important to note that a report with a poc that can be reproduced does not make it an exception to our policies. All VRP-eligible reports are expected to contain a POC and steps to reproduce, and be security issues that can be reproduced and validated. This does not mean they are all reward eligible. If a report is a duplicate of previously reported issues or issues known to us by clusterfuzz or other documented means, they are not reward eligible. 



<span class="line"><!---->, it is important to note that a report with a poc that can be reproduced does not make it an exception to our policies. All VRP-eligible reports are expected to contain a POC and steps to reproduce, and be security issues that can be reproduced and validated. This does not mean they are all reward eligible. If a report is a duplicate of previously reported issues or issues known to us by clusterfuzz or other documented means, they are not reward eligible. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I want to convey that we appreciate the effort to finding and reporting security bugs, however, we do have to stand by our policies. The VRP exists to receive reports of issues that are helpful to us in discovering issues that are impact or would impact users. Reports of issues in trunk/head due to short term regressions from ongoing work and consistently collides with our fuzzer coverage does not meet that goal. 



<span class="line"><!---->I want to convey that we appreciate the effort to finding and reporting security bugs, however, we do have to stand by our policies. The VRP exists to receive reports of issues that are helpful to us in discovering issues that are impact or would impact users. Reports of issues in trunk/head due to short term regressions from ongoing work and consistently collides with our fuzzer coverage does not meet that goal. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I hope this help explain the situation here. Please feel free to reach out on-bug or directly via email with any questions.



<span class="line"><!---->I hope this help explain the situation here. Please feel free to reach out on-bug or directly via email with any questions.<!----></span>

        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
